    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_328319683" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/328319683" />
    <a title="Megan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3388215-megan"><img alt="Megan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1373331875p2/3388215.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/328319683?book_show_action=true">May 11, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Megan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Megan" href="/user/show/3388215-megan">Megan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer328319683" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9784733059661871183"><b>Review goes live on <a href='http://bookbrats.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>Book Brats</a> on May 1st, 2013.</b> Quotes are taken from the ARC edition and may change by the final printing.<br/><br/>There are books where the hype succeeds and the book is just as amazing as you’ve heard – and then some. And then there are books where the hype just doesn’t work and you’re left sad and shaking on the floor, wondering where things went wrong in your relationship. REBOOT was one of my most anticipated 2013 titles. Let’s just remember, though, that I have a very bad track re</span>
  <span id="freeText9784733059661871183" style="display:none"><b>Review goes live on <a href="http://bookbrats.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Book Brats</a> on May 1st, 2013.</b> Quotes are taken from the ARC edition and may change by the final printing.<br /><br />There are books where the hype succeeds and the book is just as amazing as you’ve heard – and then some. And then there are books where the hype just doesn’t work and you’re left sad and shaking on the floor, wondering where things went wrong in your relationship. REBOOT was one of my most anticipated 2013 titles. Let’s just remember, though, that I have a very bad track record with picking debuts that appeal to me and then actually liking them.<br /><br />When I finished REBOOT by Amy Tintera, closing my Kindle and turning it off, I stared at the wall and wondered, “Where did our relationship go wrong?”<br /><br /><b>A SUCCESSOR TO DIVERGENT</b><br /><br />REBOOT has more in common with DIVERGENT than I expected going into it. The similarities are obvious – for one, it’s being released the week where Divergent 3 might have been released if it hadn’t been pushed back to fall (if I remember correctly, and my memory is shoddy). It is basically DIVERGENT if the members of Dauntless were zombies who could kick butt and take names. The writing is similar, as well, which may or may not be a good thing depending on your tastes.<br /><br />REBOOT has several critical flaws which ruined the experience for me. Firstly, it favored romance as an explanation over the mythology of the world and the world building. There were plot holes and contrivances thanks to the romance. Secondly, it was extremely violent, to the point where it seemed to romanticize violence and killing for the sake of maintaining a character that had already begun to falter the moment her love interest appeared.<br /><br />Following Wren 178, a Reboot who was dead 178 minutes before she reanimated as a deadly, inhuman soldier, REBOOT is about an elite team of once-dead teenage soldiers in a world decimated by a zombifying virus called KDH controlled by a quasi-government police force tasked with rounding up criminals and KDH-afflicted people. When Callum 22 (he died for 22 minutes) shows up, though, she is curious, and Callum making mooning eyes at her doesn’t help.<br /><br />It seems to be a prevailing theme in “dystopian” fiction these days where romance is the main aspect, followed by the actual dystopian elements. And when the dystopian elements mostly seemed to be another virus, a government military force that rises to contain it, and scientists that are inherently evil, I don’t know how much of a fan I can be. REBOOT never passes the ordinary on this account.<br /><br /><b>LOVE SAVES ALL</b><br /><br />As I said, REBOOT is a romance at heart. Luckily it isn’t a love triangle. Wren is the deadliest Reboot in all of New Texas until Callum shows up, and suddenly she becomes a limp noodle. Wren suddenly starts showing all the emotions that she claims are impossible, all the while maintaining that she is still cold and unflinching. Except this can’t be rationalized by her romance, nor does she ever rationalize it. In the mythos of the world, the reader is led to believe it is impossible.<br /><br />Even in situations where they’re about to die, what do Wren and Callum do? Make out. Because that’s totally the sensible thing to do when there are guns pointed at you. And the romance I didn’t buy – Wren, cold and inhuman, and Callum, sweet and naïve (potentially a little dumb). It was not a match made in heaven, more like a match made in, “You’re strange and I like that.”<br /><br /><blockquote>It was true that all Reboots were attractive, in a way. After death, when the virus took hold and the body rebooted, the skin cleared and the body sharpened, the eyes glowed. It was like pretty with a hint of deranged.</blockquote><br /><br />So it was kind of like pretty zombies in a sense, but really, all Reboots are attractive? What if you were given the ugliest teenager alive? Would they suddenly be hot? Just wondering.<br /><br /><b>GUNS ARE AWESOME</b><br /><br />I love a good action-adventure movie, but there comes a point where I think that guns are being glorified. No, I don’t think that teens and kids become homicidal maniacs based on the media. But I do think that there is such thing as the glorification of violence. When I read REBOOT, I felt like this happened when Wren talked about hating humans, wanting to kill guards, wanting to kill people who have surrendered because humans couldn’t be trusted. And does she kill humans? Yeah, and several weren’t really up to much.<br /><br /><blockquote>Giving humans a chance was a dumb idea.</blockquote><br /><br />Another big issue I had with the first 25% of the book was extreme info-dumping. Wren would wax poetic at random times about the architecture of the building, the origins of the KDH virus, how Rebooting actually worked), and so on. And Wren also has a nifty gift for inferring correctly with no information given. It got annoying after awhile.<br /><br />The prose was alright in REBOOT – there is nothing flashy about it, nothing too exciting. The pacing was pretty damn good, though, which saves REBOOT from a dreaded one star review. Tintera does an awesome job of action and plotting, leading the story on a meandering path of twists and turns (some of which are predictable) to an inevitable conclusion that I saw from the synopsis.<br /><br />Also, for people who have read the book – I have a question. If multiple people Reboot at a certain time, how do they differentiate between Reboots if the guards call them by their numbers? Just something I noticed.<br /><br /><b>VERDICT: I really wanted to love this one, but ultimately, it fell flat with me. With nothing truly to set it apart besides a heavy emphasis on love saving the day, REBOOT is an ultimately forgettable entry into the bloated dystopian market. Skip this one.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="9784733059661871183" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer7280062052117180349">This is the first book I have absolutely flown through since reading ACOWAR, and for that it deserves 5 stars. <br/><br/>I hardly read dystopian books since they usually annoy the shit out of me, but I read this purely because I loved Amy Tintera's other series so I thought I'd give this one a go too. I was not disappointed at all! I actually loved this book so much and couldn't put it down once I started. It has been a while since a book has hooked me in so easily and this book definitely exceeded my exp</span>
  <span id="freeText7280062052117180349" style="display:none">This is the first book I have absolutely flown through since reading ACOWAR, and for that it deserves 5 stars. <br /><br />I hardly read dystopian books since they usually annoy the shit out of me, but I read this purely because I loved Amy Tintera's other series so I thought I'd give this one a go too. I was not disappointed at all! I actually loved this book so much and couldn't put it down once I started. It has been a while since a book has hooked me in so easily and this book definitely exceeded my expectations. <br /><br />Clearly, this author and I get along very well and I will continue to devour her books! There's something about her simple writing style that keeps me captivated and her snarky, witty characters always have me in stitches. <br /><br />Is this the best book in the world? Nah it's really not HOWEVER I enjoyed it so so much and it's definitely deserving of a 5 star rating. <br /><br />I'd 200% recommend this book as well as her other series starting with Ruined.</span>

<div id="review_537527365" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/537527365" />
    <a title="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library"><img alt="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1350750103p2/4551536.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/537527365?book_show_action=true">Feb 15, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" href="/user/show/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library">Maja (The Nocturnal Library)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=all-action">all-action</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=all-the-right-choices">all-the-right-choices</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=best-of-2013">best-of-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=arc-2013">arc-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=debut-author">debut-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=harper-teen">harper-teen</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=open-ending">open-ending</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=edelweiss">edelweiss</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer537527365" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6248413745936921714">Long live Amy Tintera! That was the thought that was going through my head as I was reading the last few sentences of her debut. While by no means perfect, Reboot is an absolute delight. Why? There are several reasons, really, the most important (in my opinion) being that it brings a breath of originality into an oversaturated genre. <br/><br/>The idea of Reboots’ value being measured by the number of minutes it took them to revive was truly fascinating. The longer they’re dead, the less emotional they be</span>
  <span id="freeText6248413745936921714" style="display:none">Long live Amy Tintera! That was the thought that was going through my head as I was reading the last few sentences of her debut. While by no means perfect, Reboot is an absolute delight. Why? There are several reasons, really, the most important (in my opinion) being that it brings a breath of originality into an oversaturated genre. <br><br>The idea of Reboots’ value being measured by the number of minutes it took them to revive was truly fascinating. The longer they’re dead, the less emotional they become afterwards, and when you’re a soldier, less emotions means less danger of breaking. Wren is a legend among Reboots because it took her 178 minutes to revive. Other Reboots and especially humans see her as a machine. When Callum shows up, he is her exact opposite, physically weak and emotional after being only 22 minutes dead and with most of his humanity preserved. Somehow, he gets under her skin and when the time comes to eliminate him, Wren can’t let that happen.<br><br>The worldbuilding is quite possibly what Tintera does best. A part of it seems to be inspired by favelas, and the author makes it very easy to visualize. The amount of mistrust between humans and reboots is suffocating, and combined with the poverty and fear of disease, it’s almost overwhelming. <br><br>It’s true that once you take the time to process it, Reboot loses some of its shine, but not nearly enough to make that initial delight fade completely. The complete emotional shutdown Wren experienced when she rebooted could have been used better. She got over it too quickly when she met Callum, and since it was supposed to be a consequence of being dead for so long (in other words, brain damage), it seemed a bit unrealistic that a cute boy would cure her in a matter of days.<br><br>If worldbuilding was this books strong point, the romance was its weakness. The change in Wren happened far too quickly and their connection smelled too strongly of instalove. In the first few chapters, she was portrayed as someone who feels absolutely nothing: no fear, no remorse, no pain, and certainly no love. But it took no more than two smiles from Callum to completely change her behavior. It’s true that some of her coldness remained, but the change was still too pronounced.<br><br>Nevertheless, Reboot is a debut worthy of the hype. The pacing is excellent – Tintera doesn’t allow her readers to get bored even for a second. This story has so much potential and I think I have every reason to be optimistic about the second installment. <br><br><br><a href="http://www.thenocturnallibrary.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380226536i/681142.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="6248413745936921714" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_556307153" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/556307153" />
    <a title="Melanie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10890208-melanie"><img alt="Melanie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1413275441p2/10890208.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/556307153?book_show_action=true">Mar 09, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melanie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melanie" href="/user/show/10890208-melanie">Melanie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781743315507" href="/book/show/17792514-reboot">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=action">action</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=dystopian-utopian">dystopian-utopian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=kick-ass-character">kick-ass-character</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=take-your-instant-love-and-get-lost">take-your-instant-love-and-get-lost</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=swoony-guys">swoony-guys</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=not-bad-at-all">not-bad-at-all</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer556307153" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4173641475577215109">See more reviews at <a href='http://theyabooklover.blogspot.com.au/' rel='nofollow noopener'>YA Midnight Reads</a><br/><br/><b>Thank you Allen & Unwin for sending me this copy. No compensation was given of taken to alter this review.</b><br/><br/><i>'She froze. Her eyes flew from the 178 printed on my skin to my face and she let out another shriek. <br/>No. There was no human left in me.'</i><br/><br/>Reboot jumped right in, hitting a nerve of abrupt consciousness with it's vivid descriptions and magnificent writing. For an overused genre, Tintera undertook dystopia with a new kick of originality. While no means flawle</span>
  <span id="freeText4173641475577215109" style="display:none">See more reviews at <a href="http://theyabooklover.blogspot.com.au/" rel="nofollow noopener">YA Midnight Reads</a><br><br><b>Thank you Allen &amp; Unwin for sending me this copy. No compensation was given of taken to alter this review.</b><br><br><i>'She froze. Her eyes flew from the 178 printed on my skin to my face and she let out another shriek. <br>No. There was no human left in me.'</i><br><br>Reboot jumped right in, hitting a nerve of abrupt consciousness with it's vivid descriptions and magnificent writing. For an overused genre, Tintera undertook dystopia with a new kick of originality. While no means flawless, Reboot kept me engaged throughout and certainly shocked me with the staggeringly remarkable world-building that defined this novel. <br><br>Over my months of reviewing, I've come to realise something I'm awfully critical about- the world construction, or building. Constantly, I'm scrounging for a flaw, unanswered question or unrealistic piece of information. Yet I seemed to fail to find a hint of a gap in Reboot. Basically, a Reboot is our robot in here- except we have some divergence and alterations. It was imposing to learn about what makes someone a Reboot, they are people who died then came back to life- after a certain span of time- then are barcoded by the time they took to come back to life, the longer they took to relive, the less human in terms of emotions, physicality and spirituality. <br><br>For our main character, Wren, she is the prodigy to fellow Rebooters, it took 178 minutes to be healed and up again. But on the other side of the scale is Callum, still practically human with no quick reflexes and still rather emotional, took only 22 minutes to resurrect. Yet still he manages to get on Wren's soft side. When Wren is assigned to eliminate him for his humanity and weakness, she finds herself disobeying orders for the first time ever. <br><br>Wren is the new Katniss Everdeen. Equally kick-ass and more viscous that imagined, this MC held a cold and foreboding atmosphere from the very beginning. Heck- at the beginning she was killing humans. That explains EVERYTHING. Well okay, I did have a slight issue which I shall mention further in my review. However on whole, Wren developed appreciably, and held a genuine personality and logical thinking despite it being a little too fast and uneven when Callum was introduced.<br><br><i>'I grabbed Twenty-two's arm, twisted it behind his back, and cracked it with one quick thrust. He let out a yell and jerked the arm away, cradling it against his chest.'</i><br><br>The supporting characters were just as awe-inspiring and provocative. We have the best friend, Ever. But before you roll your eyes as if, "DUH! There's always the typical best friend." this one was more believable and heart-warming. By no means was Wren a interactive character, she keeps to herself as after all, her humanity levels are relatively demolished. Without regard to, the presence of Ever's being there as 56 room-mate, trying to comprehend with Wren was loveable. Ever was a compassionate character that I adored to a large extent. <br><br>Callum 22 is not only just a random Reboot, but also he was the quickest to ever come back to life meaning he was the character that made this book feel like they were complete aliens from outer space. His jocular tone and poignant smile (which I thought was mentioned way too many times throughout) levelled out the book and kept a warmth and sympathy expand towards Callum. He was sweet, <i>human</i> and loving. <br><br>Most people on this world have an Achilles just on the back part of the ankle. It is one of the weaker, if not weakest joint in us. For Reboot, it's Achilles was the romance. Largely know as insta-love, Reboot had little buildup on the chemistry between Callum and Wren. When the story commenced, Wren was emotionless but just when Callum entered a few chapters later, I didn't quite catch much growth or gradual development in Wren's personality, to make a chemistry flower. <br><br>To sum up, Reboot was overall a satisfying read filled with originality, strong characters and tense action that kept us readers alert the entire time, there is not a single dull moment in Reboot. Gruesome and exhilarating, Tintera shows us just how much dystopia or post-apocalyptic can expand to and adore. <br><div>
<br> </div><br><div>
<br>I'm not fully sure whether you guys in the US have an equally awesome edition of Reboot as I do not own a copy but the Australian Reboot edition IS. BEAUTIFUL. So if you have not received your copy of Reboot yet, consider this epic edition.</div><br><div>
<br>﻿</div><br><br><div>
  <br>
  <a href="https://lh4.googleusercontent.com/-bxQ9Uaetcdc/UZ3Cmh0IS-I/AAAAAAAAApM/fXJeY2gHpE8/s1600/blogger-image-638302316.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img height="320" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380412666i/811591.jpg" width="240" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
  <a href="https://lh4.googleusercontent.com/-k84xxCXh0XE/UZ3ClEU2XRI/AAAAAAAAApE/pITNL4GbhXE/s640/blogger-image--274599877.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img height="320" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380412666i/811592.jpg" width="240" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</div><br><div>

This storyline definitely gave me Marie Lu vibes (Legend by her is one of my favourite books) and both books were fast paced, allowing for some great action to take place. The main character Wren dies five years ago, but rebooted in a time of 178 minutes, so she is known as </span>
  <span id="freeText4555695350087948064" style="display:none">*Read as an e-book via Scribd!*<br /><br />T/W- Violence<br /><br />I am super late to Amy's writing, but how I delayed reading Reboot I simply can't answer. All I will say is that I managed to read it in a single evening and now I need the sequel! This storyline definitely gave me Marie Lu vibes (Legend by her is one of my favourite books) and both books were fast paced, allowing for some great action to take place. The main character Wren dies five years ago, but rebooted in a time of 178 minutes, so she is known as one-seventy-eight. As part of a Reboot, bring trained as a fighter, Wren takes on a new trainee called Callum or number 22. Their interactions kickstart a chain of events that sees their worlds change forever. I really liked learning more about Wren and Callum's backgrounds. There is some violence throughout the novel, however enough tension and drama that kept me reading on until the final page. </span>

<div id="review_539514719" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/539514719" />
    <a title="caren" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4201903-caren"><img alt="caren" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1579985281p2/4201903.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/539514719?book_show_action=true">Feb 18, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="caren" class="user" itemprop="url" name="caren" href="/user/show/4201903-caren">caren</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4201903-caren?shelf=book-boyfriend">book-boyfriend</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4201903-caren?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4201903-caren?shelf=swooning-for-days">swooning-for-days</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4201903-caren?shelf=galley-arc">galley-arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4201903-caren?shelf=edelweiss">edelweiss</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer539514719" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6315078223654412443"><br/>Listen up, young adult fans! Amy Tintera’s debut, <i>Reboot</i>, is one you definitely need to get your hands on. Fast! I’m serious. It has all my favorites: badass chick? Check. Hot boy? Check. Action? Killing? Kissing? Swoons? Check, check, check, check!<br/><br/>A new and interesting twist on the current popularity of zombies brings readers into the life of Wren, who was shot five years ago and then woke up—or rebooted—after one hundred and seventy eight minutes.<br/><br/>These aren’t the zombies you’d expect, though. </span>
  <span id="freeText6315078223654412443" style="display:none"><br />Listen up, young adult fans! Amy Tintera’s debut, <i>Reboot</i>, is one you definitely need to get your hands on. Fast! I’m serious. It has all my favorites: badass chick? Check. Hot boy? Check. Action? Killing? Kissing? Swoons? Check, check, check, check!<br /><br />A new and interesting twist on the current popularity of zombies brings readers into the life of Wren, who was shot five years ago and then woke up—or rebooted—after one hundred and seventy eight minutes.<br /><br />These aren’t the zombies you’d expect, though. These reboots are stronger, faster, less emotional and, well, they don’t eat humans.<br /><br />Mostly.<br /><br />In Wren’s future, fifty states have been reduced to one. What <i>we</i> know of as Texas has become the Republic of Texas, divided into cities where humans are trying to keep the virus that’s causing their children to reboot contained. As a Reboot, Wren’s works for the “government” or HARC, as it’s known here. Her job as a reboot is to complete her assignments by bringing in criminals and sick people, to train newbies and to <i>never</i> ask questions. And as a one seventy eight, she’s pretty damn good at it. She doesn’t feel things the way the other numbers do, those below sixty whose human emotions still remain.<br /><br />That is, until a twenty-two named Callum shows up…<br /><br />From the moment they meet, Wren’s captivated by him. But he’s a twenty two, and she can’t see relating to Callum at all. Until Wren feels challenged to take him on as a newbie.<br /><br />What she doesn’t expect is that he won’t be the only one learning new things.<br /><br />In case you haven’t figured it out yet, I pretty much loved this from beginning to end. I was a little head tilty at first, but once I got into the story, I couldn’t put this one down. And Callum, he just made this book for me. Is that surprising? Probably not. BUT SERIOUSLY. He was a-freaking-dorable.<br /><br /><blockquote>”I’ll try and sleep,” he said, closing his eyes. He cracked one eye open and held his arm out to me. “Want to come closer?”<br /><br />“I can’t. One of us has to stay up and keep watch.”<br /><br />“One cuddle. Maybe two. Fifteen, max.”<br /><br />“Callum,” I said with a laugh. “Go to sleep.”<br /><br />“All right,” he said with an exaggerated sigh, a smile twitching his lips.</blockquote><br /><br />See? Adorable. Callum totally earned himself a top spot on my Book Boyfriend shelf with his personality, his chivalry and his sweetness. So I’ll say this again: I loved this book, and I absolutely cannot freaking wait for the continuation to this series! It doesn’t have a title yet, but I’m going to go ahead and start referring to it as <i>Reservation</i>. You’ll understand once you hurry up and go read it. ;)<br /><br /><i>*** ARC Provided via Edelweiss in exchange for an honest review. ***</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="6315078223654412443" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2041479373" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2041479373" />
    <a title="Daiane" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32806732-daiane"><img alt="Daiane" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1457143503p2/32806732.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2041479373?book_show_action=true">Jun 26, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Daiane" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Daiane" href="/user/show/32806732-daiane">Daiane</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2041479373" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9716942074021857040"><b>Actual Rating:</b> 3.5<br/><br/>I have to confess that the blurb didn't attracted me that much but I love Amy Tintera's writing so I just left it on my kindle until I read it. I found out that I'm really attracted to her stories. Still, this one wasn't that awesome. <br/><br/><b>
  <i>“There’s some human left in you, ain’t there?” she asked, craning her neck to look at the number above the bar code on my wrist.<br/>She froze. Her eyes flew from the 178 printed on my skin to my face and she let out another shriek.<br/>No. There was no </i></b></span>
  <span id="freeText9716942074021857040" style="display:none"><b>Actual Rating:</b> 3.5<br /><br />I have to confess that the blurb didn't attracted me that much but I love Amy Tintera's writing so I just left it on my kindle until I read it. I found out that I'm really attracted to her stories. Still, this one wasn't that awesome. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>“There’s some human left in you, ain’t there?” she asked, craning her neck to look at the number above the bar code on my wrist.<br />She froze. Her eyes flew from the 178 printed on my skin to my face and she let out another shriek.<br />No. There was no human left in me.</i>
</b><br /><br />The main character, Wren, is a real badass. She is like a cold robot that has the highest rank among the reboots (those who died and came back to life. Kinda like a zombie, but human...?). <br /><br /><b>
  <i>Do that thing where you look blank, like you have no feelings at all.”<br />“I think that’s just my face.”</i>
</b><br /><br />But when she meets Callum, the lowest in the rank, she just.... Feels. It's not a problem to feel a little, but she is just a scary little girl blushing. Like seriously? She didn't care about the world for five years and suddenly she is all caring? It's just a little strange...<br /> <br /><b>
  <i>“He could punish you for that,”<br />“Do you want me to?” Leb asked, eyeing Twenty-two. He didn’t reach for the stick.<br />“No,” I replied. Every Reboot in the shuttle stared at me. I focused on Twenty-two again.<br />“Should I be insulted that you hesitated?” he asked with a smile.<br />“I can still change my mind.”<br />“How will you tell him? He stopped talking. Apparently that means we’re only allowed to talk to one another again.”<br />“I will find a stick and beat you myself when we land.”<br />“Promise?”</i>
</b><br /><br />Callum is cute and all too funny. Even though he is really low he still tries his best. But I still thought he was missing something. I couldn't exactly name what, but it was like HE was the Mary Sue. Don't take me wrong, it's not like the man has to save the woman and he has to be stronger than her. It's just that he was almost useless and this bothered me. Gosh, how couldn't he stay still for a moment? That bothered me like hell!!<br /><br />Anyway, it was a good and fast read and I still love Amy's creativity and for sure will keep reading her books. But this one is not one of my favorites. </span>

<div id="review_1652249387" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1652249387" />
    <a title="Vivianne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33012562-vivianne"><img alt="Vivianne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1580677327p2/33012562.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1652249387?book_show_action=true">Jul 11, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vivianne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vivianne" href="/user/show/33012562-vivianne">Vivianne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9789000350223" href="/book/show/30653472-reboot">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33012562-vivianne?shelf=z-3-stars">z-3-stars</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1652249387" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13430156092352291284">I didn’t really have an expectation for this book, but chose to read it because it has been on my shelves a while and I was looking for something quick before going on my holiday to French. But unfortunately I wasn’t that impressed by it. I felt like I’ve read this plot so many times in another book, I wasn’t captivated by the writing style and I got annoyed with the main character and the romance. However I did really enjoy the ‘rebooting’ concept and the beginning of this book was rather enter</span>
  <span id="freeText13430156092352291284" style="display:none">I didn’t really have an expectation for this book, but chose to read it because it has been on my shelves a while and I was looking for something quick before going on my holiday to French. But unfortunately I wasn’t that impressed by it. I felt like I’ve read this plot so many times in another book, I wasn’t captivated by the writing style and I got annoyed with the main character and the romance. However I did really enjoy the ‘rebooting’ concept and the beginning of this book was rather entertaining. <br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1652249387 " rel="nofollow noopener">Reboot: 3 stars</a><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2129407041?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1%20" rel="nofollow noopener">Rebel: 3 stars</a><br /><br /><u>
  <b>Design (3,5 stars) </b>
</u><br />I really like the Dutch version of this book (for a change). They really fit with the contents in this book, it has an barcode forming the end of all the papers. I do like the colors of this book but I hate the image of the person on the background. <br /><br /><u>
  <b>Concept (4,0 stars) </b>
</u><br />The concept of the rebooting was something I really enjoyed in this book and unfortunately it was one of the only original things about this book. I was intrigued by it and I was curious how Tintera could write a plot in less than 300 pages.<br /><br /><u>
  <b>Start of the book (4,5 stars) </b>
</u><br />I REALLY enjoyed the beginning of this book, and I was surprised how quick this book read. I was certain I would finish it within a day with my current pace. The writing style was quick and easy, I liked Wren and found her to display a reboot quite well, I really enjoyed the plot and was intrigued by the world building and the rebooting system. <br /><br /><u>
  <b>The writing style (2,5 stars) </b>
</u><br /><i>Note: read in Dutch.</i><br />In the beginning I had a bit of trouble with the past tense that this book is being told in. It had been a while since I read a book like that and I struggled with the difference between what currently was happening and what was a memory or a flashback. But later on in the book I got used to it. The writing style was rather quick and easy. Too easy if you ask me, I like a bit of a challenge and this made me a bit bored. Furthermore there weren’t really beautiful quotes or other things about this book that made it special, it was average (could be because of the translation). The way some scenes are written was almost without feeling, it didn’t come across sometimes and though I understand because Wren is a reboot but also later in the book with some romance scenes the writing was really plain. A thing that got me a tat annoyed was writing the numbers (the minutes that people had died) full out in letters instead of numbers. I also got annoyed with some errors in the language and the way things are written didn’t appeal to me. The descriptions used for the surroundings and descriptions where really superficial. I would have rather had that the book was about 50 pages longer with some more explanations. <br /><br /><u>
  <b>The world building (2,5 stars) </b>
</u><br />Like I said before, I was really intrigued by the world building concept. I found the idea of the reboots fascinating and I really enjoyed reading about Wren’s time at HARC. However my problems starts with the concept of this whole society. We know NOTHING about the ruling party, if I look back on it. How is it founded? Why? Who is the leader? What year is it? My other problem is that it was so cliché, I had read about it like a hundred times in every other YA dystopian book. And this one wasn’t even executed that well. I still have so many questions about the experiments they did on the lower numbers. It just didn’t make any sense, why make them into flesh eating monsters? And also just keeping this citizens prisoners in their own city? How would someone accept this? How can they even accept that their child is taken away from them? Some things do not add up with instinct and morals that a basic human has. But also this virus (another cliché ya book thing), where did it come from? What kind of virus is it? Why are adult reboots different then teens? Why does this virus make people reboot? There wasn’t any history given about this and it got me so annoyed. <br /><br /><u>
  <b>Main Character (2,5 stars) </b>
</u><br />In the beginning I enjoyed Wren, I enjoyed her ruthlessness and found her badass. But I did found her underdeveloped and towards the end I got annoyed with her choices and thoughts. And I think that is one of the reasons I didn’t really connect with Wren. Another reason was that I didn’t really understand her mind. It was so conflicting at times what she thought and did and why. For example in the beginning of the book is told that Wren is the fastest, strongest reboot out there is. Then a few pages further she is trembling on her legs because some minor thing and even further she is so scared she can’t even move. Another example is that the higher the minutes you died the more emotionless you are. So Wren with her 178 minutes is supposed to be totally emotionless. But she blushes over the smallest things, makes friendships, cares about reboots and does have emotions. It was super incoherent. <br />And also her ‘transformation’ throughout this book was super unrealistic. She just sees a pretty boy, someone who’s being nice to her and falls for that and all of a sudden her whole morals and thoughts shift?!? Okay I understand that after the thing with Ever she understood Harc was really wrong. BUT I still don’t understand that someone can change from being so badass in the beginning towards something so dependent on someone and scared towards the ending. I didn’t like how she acted in the slum of Austin, how she collapsed in the woods. Since in the beginning I was really impressed by this book for having a strong female lead and a mc who did not depend on a male character. But yeahhh I was wrong… <br /><br /><u>
  <b>Other characters (3,5 stars) </b>
</u><br />I really enjoyed Ever, she was so spunky and fun and I loved her and Wren’s friendship. I also really liked Callum, and how he made Wren feel (in the beginning). He made so many funny comments. But towards the end he also started to annoy me.<br />Adina was a character that was one of the most flawed. They walk to her and they start to fight and it takes about 2 words to convince her to come with her even though she is almost programmed to work for Harc… Her character was really underdeveloped and was just there to serve as the role to ‘save someone’.<br /><br /><u>
  <b>Romance (2,0 stars) </b>
</u><br />I felt the romance took over the whole story. The blurb sounds like an action packed, badass story. But towards the ending, the only focus was on the relationship between Callum and Wren, and that annoyed me. I also found them super conflicting and didn’t feel anything between them. Their relationship seemed super superficial and I just didn’t care for it at all. <br /><br /><u>
  <b>Plot (2,5 stars) </b>
</u><br />I extremely enjoyed the plot in the beginning . It was action packed, original (the rebooting and stuff), enjoyable and fast paced. Maybe a bit too quick considering the fact that this book is not even 300 pages long, I would have liked to see some more scenes from previous missions since I really enjoyed those. Everything already went wrong on page 50 and I would have liked to have some more getting to know to the whole reboot system and to Wren. I enjoyed it so much that Wren started to find out what was wrong with the system and with her and Callum. There are literally two scenes that made me tear up; Ever being shot and when Wren needed to take of her shirt. <br />It was later in the book that I started to have a problem with the pacing. Wren and Callum escape, and I understand that they didn’t have time because Meyer was watching them and yada yada, but in my opinion this all happened in an eye blink. And though I enjoyed this action packed scene it was unrealistic. My other problem with the plot from that point was that it wasn’t original anymore. It reminded me of Matched, the Hunger Games, Divergent, Boy 7, Delirium etc… All these book have the aspect of the mc escaping ‘the big bad government’ towards an rebellion somewhere. It felt like I’d already read this and I was kind a getting bored. <br />Another problem was that there weren’t enough twists, nothing surprising happens, noting shocking and nothing that made me really love this book happened. Not one person dies, there is no betrayal, no backstabbing, no twist. It was just so predictable.<br /><br /><u>
  <b>The ending (1,5 stars) </b>
</u><br />The ending was a letdown for me. But since I would only start to repeat myself if I talk about it here real quick some points; predictable, didn’t care who lived or died, boring, strange choices by Wren, odd action scenes, no setbacks (even though this was an ‘impossible mission’ when they talked with the humans), no casualties, more annoying things by Wren, weird make out scene during a shuttle flight when Wren is the pilot, the last words.<br />There just isn’t a thing about this ending that makes me want to read the next book. But I already own it so I’ll probably read it. Someday… when I feel like it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13430156092352291284" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1438112653?book_show_action=true">Nov 09, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Simona B" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Simona B" href="/user/show/5312173-simona-b">Simona B</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780062217080" href="/book/show/18090051-reboot">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=in-english">in-english</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=2000">2000</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1438112653" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12674026140738265212"><b>2.5<br/><br/>“I think people immediately assumed I was yours so they stayed far away.' He met my eyes and smiled. 'I was. I am.' He leaned forward and brushed his lips to mine. 'Yours.” </b><br/><br/> <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1396813681ra/9190000.gif' width='420' height='220' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>No.<br/><br/>But she? What does she do? She melts.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1451565100ra/17559087.gif' width='420' height='220' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/> <i>Figures</i>.<br/><br/>I was first drawn to this book because the <b>heroine</b> sounded like a sort of icy robot, emotionless and not human at all. And then it turns out she's just a <b>softie</b> even <b>softier</b> than an average teen-aged girl. I just can't.<br/><br/>Maybe my two stars are a little too strict, but I can't</span>
  <span id="freeText12674026140738265212" style="display:none"><b>2.5<br><br>“I think people immediately assumed I was yours so they stayed far away.' He met my eyes and smiled. 'I was. I am.' He leaned forward and brushed his lips to mine. 'Yours.” </b><br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1396813681ra/9190000.gif" width="420" height="220" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>No.<br><br>But she? What does she do? She melts.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1451565100ra/17559087.gif" width="420" height="220" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br> <i>Figures</i>.<br><br>I was first drawn to this book because the <b>heroine</b> sounded like a sort of icy robot, emotionless and not human at all. And then it turns out she's just a <b>softie</b> even <b>softier</b> than an average teen-aged girl. I just can't.<br><br>Maybe my two stars are a little too strict, but I can't think of anything positive to say about this book. There is nothing truly remarkable in here. The <b>plot</b> is so simple that my little eight year-old brother could have come up with it. The <b>writing</b> is right above the acceptable, and vague and imprecise most of the time. There is no depth, no adrenaline and no thrill. There is just <i>nothing</i>. I can't bring myself to give a higher rating because this book gave me no reason to do so. It's just so <b>flat</b>, so <b>naive</b>. Everything in this story is smooth, easy, no-sweat. It's as if the laws of the universe bend to let our heroes go on without a problem. <br><br>An example of 'what on earth is this supposed to mean': I've still not understood why no one among the rebels wanted to go retrieve Addie. It's not like they had to fight against an army. They just had to approach her, hand her the tracker, and then she could even do everything by herself. I don't see the danger of such a mission, but <i>no</i>, it's extremely dangerous and so they have to hire a Reboot to do it. Otherwise, how could the protagonist fit in the plot?<br>Now find the courage to tell me this is not stupid.<br><br>And I am even more sorry because <b>I truly wanted to like this</b>; the premise was kind of interesting and I was extremely intrigued by the main character we were promised. <br>You can't believe how<b> disappointed </b>I am.</span>

<div id="review_636844464" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/636844464" />
    <a title="Neil (or bleed)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14057379-neil-or-bleed"><img alt="Neil (or bleed)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572821192p2/14057379.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/636844464?book_show_action=true">Jun 09, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

<div id="review_2399782807" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2399782807" />
    <a title="Maggie ☘" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/40477684-maggie"><img alt="Maggie ☘" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1591529603p2/40477684.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2399782807?book_show_action=true">May 26, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maggie ☘" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maggie ☘" href="/user/show/40477684-maggie">Maggie ☘</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40477684-maggie?shelf=meh-reads">meh-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40477684-maggie?shelf=dystopia-sci-fi">dystopia-sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40477684-maggie?shelf=irritating-heroines">irritating-heroines</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40477684-maggie?shelf=overrated-or-disappointing">overrated-or-disappointing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40477684-maggie?shelf=unpopular-opinions">unpopular-opinions</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2399782807" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10176002772714570825">This is what I call 'false advertising'. It's no kick ass, the heroine is just a blushing idiot doing everything (and I mean EVERYTHING) for the love interest only. She doesn't have some greater realization, doesn't fight for her believes or whatewer. No, she did everything just for the love interest, even though she knew him for just a few weeks.. <br/><br/>It's like: How to Not write a Dystopia in five easy steps. You don't even have to try to be original or anything..<br/><br/>The author took everything that is </span>
  <span id="freeText10176002772714570825" style="display:none">This is what I call 'false advertising'. It's no kick ass, the heroine is just a blushing idiot doing everything (and I mean EVERYTHING) for the love interest only. She doesn't have some greater realization, doesn't fight for her believes or whatewer. No, she did everything just for the love interest, even though she knew him for just a few weeks.. <br /><br />It's like: How to Not write a Dystopia in five easy steps. You don't even have to try to be original or anything..<br /><br />The author took everything that is generic and overdone in the genre and stuffed it all into this. It's like Reboot is trying way too hard to be like all the other hit dystopians - we're mostly talking Hunger Games here, 'cause this was like a BAD copycat of that series - but fails misarably. It's generic, balnd, boring and stuffed with cringe worthy romance that tries way too hard to have the dynamics of Katniss/Peeta, which it of course doesn't because the characters couldn't be more one dimensional than they are. Everything about this book is one diamensional - the world, the plot and the writing as well. The distant idea bahind the Rebooting was somewhat eh... new, but was just buried by all that terrible execution and awfuly boring romance. Just STOP kissing for a minute ok?? Don't you need to take a breath? (Apparently not in the second half of this shitty book). <br /><br />I'm baffled by how much Reboot was hyped up when it came out. Like I'm not the biggest fan of Divergent (hated the sequels) or Legend (great dystopia but didn't feel connected to the characters at all), but they are a treasure compared to THIS. And let's not forget Hunger Games (which is probably the only dystopian series that is my among my all time favourites) - Reboot tries so much to be like that trilogy - especially with the romance, the love interest and how the 'typical gender roles' in the romance aspect of the story *heavy sarcasm* were kind of reversed here - but utterly FAILS. Callum is no new Peeta. Also, a day after finishing I already forgot the name of the MC..</span>
  <a data-text-id="10176002772714570825" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_645521707" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/645521707" />
    <a title="Emily" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16362475-emily"><img alt="Emily" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1559946867p2/16362475.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/645521707?book_show_action=true">Jun 19, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily" href="/user/show/16362475-emily">Emily</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16362475-emily?shelf=dnf">dnf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16362475-emily?shelf=couldn-t-finish">couldn-t-finish</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer645521707" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14242590766753957773"><i> Five years ago, Wren Connolly was shot three times in the chest. After 178 minutes she came back as a Reboot: stronger, faster, able to heal, and less emotional. The longer Reboots are dead, the less human they are when they return. <br/><br/>Wren’s favorite part of the job is training new Reboots, but her latest newbie is the worst she’s ever seen. As a 22, Callum Reyes is practically human. His reflexes are too slow, he’s always asking questions, and his ever-present smile is freaking her out. Yet ther</i></span>
  <span id="freeText14242590766753957773" style="display:none"><i> Five years ago, Wren Connolly was shot three times in the chest. After 178 minutes she came back as a Reboot: stronger, faster, able to heal, and less emotional. The longer Reboots are dead, the less human they are when they return. <br><br>Wren’s favorite part of the job is training new Reboots, but her latest newbie is the worst she’s ever seen. As a 22, Callum Reyes is practically human. His reflexes are too slow, he’s always asking questions, and his ever-present smile is freaking her out. Yet there’s something about him she can’t ignore. When Callum refuses to follow an order, Wren is given one last chance to get him in line—or she’ll have to eliminate him. Wren has never disobeyed before and knows if she does, she’ll be eliminated, too. But she has also never felt as alive as she does around Callum. </i><br><br>I don't even know why I thought this book was gonna be so good. The blurb has INSTA-LOVE written in big bold letters all over it. And I'd also really like to point out how it says that Wren 178 is stronger, faster, able to heal, and <b> less emotional </b>. Then HOW COME Wren always felt guilty, sad or angry? Why did she act like a love-struck fool 75% of the time (as far as I read)? Why did she blush every time Callum the Nobody looked at her? You know what was emotionless (and boring)? The writing!<br><br><i> <b> "When the shuttle landed, I trailed out last. My trembling legs didn't work right anymore. I fell behind as the other Reboots marched across the roof and down the stairs." </b> </i><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380425978ra/850611.gif" width="300" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br>That's nice.<br><br>The love-interest, Callum was pretty much an average human guy, full of moral speeches and "uplifting" talks. Most of the time I was just sitting there hoping he would shut up. "No I won't kill him!", "No, I won't hit you!", "I can't let them turn me into a monster!". OKAY CALLUM, WE GET IT. STOP. NOW. PLEASE. Jeez, calm down. <br><br>And there was no world-building. What was the virus? Where did it come from? Was it accidentally unleashed or? It felt like I was just thrown right into a situation without knowing anything about it, and no one would tell me.<br><br>I dunno, maybe there was something about this book that I just didn't <i> get </i>? If it was, please do tell me, because I'd really like to know. Might give this book another shot another time couse I really do hate not being able to finish books. <br><br><b> DNF-ed at 68%. 1 star. </b></span>
  <a data-text-id="14242590766753957773" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_827640617" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/827640617" />
    <a title="Drew" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22104588-drew"><img alt="Drew" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1498412758p2/22104588.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/827640617?book_show_action=true">Jan 18, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Drew" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Drew" href="/user/show/22104588-drew">Drew</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22104588-drew?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22104588-drew?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer827640617" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14967297005888490967">3 1/2 stars. <b>"YA dystopians."</b> If you're anything like me then you probably give an involuntary shudder when you hear those words. It's such an overhyped—perhaps the <i>most</i> overhyped—genre, and aren't you tired of seeing those endless cloning movie adaptions?<br/><br/>Thankfully, I think this is a genre that has died down. All the newest authors don't seem as crazy to write the next Hunger Games, but the damage was done—millions of dystopian books were published and most of them were terrible copies of each </span>
  <span id="freeText14967297005888490967" style="display:none">3 1/2 stars. <b>"YA dystopians."</b> If you're anything like me then you probably give an involuntary shudder when you hear those words. It's such an overhyped—perhaps the <i>most</i> overhyped—genre, and aren't you tired of seeing those endless cloning movie adaptions?<br /><br />Thankfully, I think this is a genre that has died down. All the newest authors don't seem as crazy to write the next Hunger Games, but the damage was done—millions of dystopian books were published and most of them were terrible copies of each other.<br /><br /><i>Reboot</i> is one of those dystopian books, but surprisingly <b>I was able to really enjoy it.</b> Set in a future Texas where a plague has broken out, scientists have discovered a way to revive dead people. But the longer it takes for them to wake up, the less emotional, the less <i>human</i> they become. Wren has a record of Rebooting after 178 minutes and is one of the most emotionless, robot-like killers.<br /><br />One thing I really liked was the <b>healthy portrayal of romance.</b> A male love interest who isn't a jerk and a relationship where both people respect each other? Whoop whoop!<br /><br />There is a big theme of Wren being small and female and how people underestimate her. But she quickly shocks them by showing them how powerful she is. I really liked the <b>slightly feminist undercurrent.</b> Plus, Wren was just an awesome main character.<br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>“You’re right,” I said. “I should have picked One-twenty-one. But now I’m stuck with you, so I suggest you quit your whining and pull it together.”</blockquote>
</i><br />This book wasn't perfect. I would have liked to know more about the process of creating Reboots. How exactly did the scientists revive dead people? This was a detail that didn't bother me much, but I think it would have made the story stronger had it been included.<br /><br />There were explorations about what makes someone human. How much emotion is necessary before people start to accept you? The Reboots were desensitized to emotions but were still proud of who they were: a new turn of technology and science.<br /><br />This was such a cool, action-packed sci-fi and a well executed idea. <b>It was one dystopian that stood out among the others.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="14967297005888490967" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer403282645" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer5888877972557447605"><b>3.5 stars</b> Really enjoyed this one--original premise, measured action sequences, a ruthless, non-emotional heroine who is pretty much a killing machine, and an unusual boy/girl dynamic that doesn't follow the typical relationship expectations. A lot of stuff packed into a fairly short book, and a strong debut. Looking forward to book two!<br/><br/>Recommended for fans of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10194494.False_Memory__False_Memory___1_' title='False Memory (False Memory, #1) by Dan Krokos' rel='nofollow noopener'>False Memory</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13335037.Divergent__Divergent___1_' title='Divergent (Divergent, #1) by Veronica Roth' rel='nofollow noopener'>Divergent</a>, and other action-oriented sci fi thrillers.</span>
  <span id="freeText5888877972557447605" style="display:none"><b>3.5 stars</b> Really enjoyed this one--original premise, measured action sequences, a ruthless, non-emotional heroine who is pretty much a killing machine, and an unusual boy/girl dynamic that doesn't follow the typical relationship expectations. A lot of stuff packed into a fairly short book, and a strong debut. Looking forward to book two!<br /><br />Recommended for fans of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10194494.False_Memory__False_Memory___1_" title="False Memory (False Memory, #1) by Dan Krokos" rel="nofollow noopener">False Memory</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13335037.Divergent__Divergent___1_" title="Divergent (Divergent, #1) by Veronica Roth" rel="nofollow noopener">Divergent</a>, and other action-oriented sci fi thrillers.</span>

<div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground">Readers also enjoyed</h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent"><div class='bookCarousel'>
<div class='carouselRow' style='width: 3600px'>
<ul>
<li class='cover' id='bookCover_16135109'>
<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16135109-impostor"><img alt="Impostor (Variants, #1)" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1370018807l/16135109._SX98_.jpg" />
</a>

  
<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('j+MnpADtbcEpeAsecVg8TqpTyqxt0buJ4uQE2fWWssHBgYJcgqGuCto5pmfwpxKtNiXcRxJtw2IVWQ0kCNCOrw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('XlppsaK0LwfnFNsDcNXJGdap7iJIVKkISBB4stPHeRsQOMxJIPjszBRVdnrxKuf6St/4yTfo0eO/rXFPLoFFdQ==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>
